          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript.


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

        output: >2-
           In this study, we explore the role of gene-gene interactions in complex traits and disease progression. We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. Our results show that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating co-expressed gene groups, PhenoPLIER contextualizes genetic associations and reveals potential targets missed by single-gene strategies, providing a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.

          Keywords: genetic studies, functional genomics, gene co-expression,
          therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering of complex traits

          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

        output: >2-
           Understanding the complex interplay between genes in specific contexts is crucial for elucidating how they influence traits and for developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have provided insights into the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms, modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions are vital in understanding disease origin and progression. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER's incorporation of co-expressed gene groups provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations and reveals potential targets missed by single-gene strategies, shedding light on disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          Explanation: 

          1) The context is established with the understanding that
          comprehending gene interactions in specific contexts is essential for
          understanding complex traits and developing new therapies. It also
          highlights the limitations of current methods such as
          transcriptome-wide association studies. 2) The content introduces
          PhenoPLIER, a computational approach mapping gene-trait associations
          and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
          representation for joint analysis, based on modules of genes with
          similar expression patterns. It presents the observation that diseases
          are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
          cell types and that PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease
          pairs and infers mechanisms of action. 3) The conclusion emphasizes
          how PhenoPLIER's incorporation of co-expressed gene groups provides a
          novel framework for interpreting genetic associations, revealing
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies, thereby shedding
          light on disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

      vars: *ref_1
      response:
        output: ' Genes collaborate in specific contexts to perform their functions, and understanding how they influence complex traits necessitates elucidating expression regulation across varying conditions. This knowledge is vital for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped elucidate the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms; however, modern models of the architecture of complex traits suggest that gene-gene interactions play a critical role in disease origin and progression. Here, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discover that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, providing valuable insights into disease etiology and drug mechanisms.'

        output: ' Genes function in concert with one another in specific contexts to carry out their roles. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates a mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation across various conditions. This insight is essential for developing innovative therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have elucidated the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms; however, contemporary models of the architecture of complex traits propose that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease onset and progression. We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational methodology that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of co-expressed genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Utilizing a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discover that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, shedding light on disease etiology and drug mechanisms.'

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

      response:
        output: >2-
           Genes collaborate in specific contexts to perform their functions, and understanding how they influence complex traits necessitates a comprehensive grasp of expression regulation across different conditions. This knowledge is essential for developing novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have been instrumental in elucidating the roles of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture propose that gene-gene interactions are crucial in determining disease origin and progression. In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of co-expressed genes across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary, by considering groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, providing valuable insights into disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          In this revised abstract, we have made improvements in grammar,
          clarity, and organization, while maintaining the essential ideas and
          findings of the original manuscript. The title and keywords have also
          been adjusted to better reflect the content of the revised abstract.

           In the field of genomics, understanding how genes interact with one another in specific contexts is crucial for deciphering their functions and roles in complex traits. This insight is critical for developing new therapies; however, current transcriptome-wide association studies primarily focus on individual genes rather than gene-gene interactions. Modern models predict that these interactions play a significant role in disease origin and progression. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. In a CRISPR screen analyzing lipid regulation, we found that functionally important players lacked associations but were prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Consequently, our approach was accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, highlighting the importance of considering group interactions rather than individual genes in disease etiology and therapeutic development.

          into a common latent representation for joint analysis. Finally, the
          conclusion interprets the results by highlighting how PhenoPLIER can
          contextualize genetic associations, reveal potential targets missed by
          single-gene strategies, and provide a novel framework for interpreting
          genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.

Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis based on modules of co-expressed genes.           traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

           We present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that synthesizes gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent space for joint analysis. Recognizing that genes interact with one another in specific contexts to carry out their functions is essential for understanding the role of these interactions in complex traits and developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the contribution of individual genes to disease-related mechanisms, contemporary models suggest that gene-gene interactions are pivotal in determining disease initiation and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is grounded in modules of co-expressed genes across various conditions. Our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action.           Here's the revised abstract with improved grammar and readability:


          We present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that unites gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent space for joint analysis. Understanding how genes interact with
          each other in specific contexts is vital for elucidating the role of
          these interactions in complex traits and developing new therapies.
          While transcriptome-wide association studies have provided insights
          into the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms,
          modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions are crucial in
          determining disease onset and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation
          is based on modules of co-expressed genes across various conditions.
          Our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and
          elucidates mechanisms of action. When analyzing lipid regulation using
          a CRISPR screen, we find that functionally significant players are not
          associated but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In summary, by integrating co-expressed gene groups,
          PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and identify
          potential targets missed by single-gene approaches. PhenoPLIER offers
          a novel perspective for interpreting genetic associations through the
          lens of gene modules, facilitating the discovery of new therapeutic
          targets and elucidating drug mechanisms in the context of disease
          etiology.


          By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can
          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed
          by single-gene strategies. This innovative framework provides a novel
          approach for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of
          gene modules, which could lead to the discovery of new therapeutic
          targets and elucidation of drug mechanisms in relation to disease
          etiology.

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations

          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes
          act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
          functions. Determining how these genes influence complex traits
          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in

          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with

          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

           We present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that synthesizes gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for integrated analysis. Genes operate in concert within specific contexts to carry out their functions; understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates comprehending expression regulation across various conditions. This comprehension is vital for designing novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have elucidated the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of the architecture of complex traits propose that gene-gene interactions are crucial for disease emergence and progression. In summary, integrating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and uncover potential targets overlooked by single-gene approaches. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for decoding genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, facilitating the elucidation of disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown

          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

           Genes collaborate to perform their functions in specific contexts, necessitating a comprehensive understanding of gene expression regulation across diverse conditions. This insight is essential for the development of novel therapies and elucidating disease-relevant mechanisms. While transcriptome-wide association studies have revealed the roles of individual genes, modern models emphasize the importance of gene-gene interactions in disease origin and progression. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is built on gene modules with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We find that diseases are significantly linked to gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation, we discover that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER, highlighting its potential in identifying therapeutic targets and repurposing drugs.

          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER.

Understanding these interactions is crucial for developing new therapies and unraveling disease-relevant mechanisms. While transcriptome-wide association studies have revealed the role of individual genes, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a vital role in disease origin and progression. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infer mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discover that functionally important players lacking associations are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. This research highlights the importance of considering gene-gene interactions for better understanding disease etiology and drug mechanisms, ultimately advancing therapeutic targets and drug repurposing strategies.'

        output: >2-
           Genes function in coordinated networks to execute their roles, necessitating an understanding of expression regulation across different conditions for deciphering the influence of these genes on complex traits. Such insights are crucial for developing novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have elucidated the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture propose that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease origin and progression. In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for simultaneous analysis. This representation is grounded on modules of co-expressed genes across the same conditions. We observe significant associations between diseases and gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER demonstrates high accuracy in predicting known drug-disease pairs and elucidating mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized within trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.

          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

            text: ' Genes collaborate in specific contexts to perform their functions, and understanding how they influence complex traits necessitates elucidating expression regulation across varying conditions. This knowledge is vital for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped elucidate the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms; however, modern models of the architecture of complex traits suggest that gene-gene interactions play a critical role in disease origin and progression. Here, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discover that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, providing valuable insights into disease etiology and drug mechanisms.'

            text: ' Genes function in concert with one another in specific contexts to carry out their roles. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates a mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation across various conditions. This insight is essential for developing innovative therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have elucidated the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms; however, contemporary models of the architecture of complex traits propose that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease onset and progression. We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational methodology that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of co-expressed genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We find that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Utilizing a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discover that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, shedding light on disease etiology and drug mechanisms.'

              ---
               Genes collaborate in specific contexts to perform their functions, and understanding how they influence complex traits necessitates a comprehensive grasp of expression regulation across different conditions. This knowledge is essential for developing novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have been instrumental in elucidating the roles of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture propose that gene-gene interactions are crucial in determining disease origin and progression. In this study, we present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of co-expressed genes across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary, by considering groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, providing valuable insights into disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              clarity, and organization, while maintaining the essential ideas
              and findings of the original manuscript. The title and keywords
              have also been adjusted to better reflect the content of the
              revised abstract.

            text: >2-
               In the field of genomics, understanding how genes interact with one another in specific contexts is crucial for deciphering their functions and roles in complex traits. This insight is critical for developing new therapies; however, current transcriptome-wide association studies primarily focus on individual genes rather than gene-gene interactions. Modern models predict that these interactions play a significant role in disease origin and progression. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. By incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. In a CRISPR screen analyzing lipid regulation, we found that functionally important players lacked associations but were prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Consequently, our approach was accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, highlighting the importance of considering group interactions rather than individual genes in disease etiology and therapeutic development.

              to understand gene-gene interactions for developing new therapies.

              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
              analysis. Finally, the conclusion interprets the results by
              highlighting how PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations, reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies, and provide a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations through the lens of gene modules.

            text: ' Genes function in concert with one another within specific contexts to perform their roles. Understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates elucidating the mechanisms of expression regulation across different conditions. This knowledge is critical for developing novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have aided in uncovering the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of the architecture of complex traits suggest that gene-gene interactions are vital to understanding disease etiology and progression. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe significant associations between diseases and gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized within trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, providing valuable insights into disease etiology and drug mechanisms.'

            text: >2-
               Understanding the interplay of genes in specific contexts is crucial for unraveling their roles in complex traits and developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have helped elucidate the role of individual genes, modern models emphasize the importance of gene-gene interactions in disease origin and progression. Here, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis based on modules of co-expressed genes. Our results demonstrate the significance of gene modules expressed in relevant cell types for diseases and PhenoPLIER's accuracy in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we found that functionally important players lacking associations were prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER's incorporation of co-expressed gene groups allows for the contextualization of genetic associations, revealing potential targets missed by single-gene strategies and providing a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through gene modules.

              ---
               We present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that synthesizes gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent space for joint analysis. Recognizing that genes interact with one another in specific contexts to carry out their functions is essential for understanding the role of these interactions in complex traits and developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the contribution of individual genes to disease-related mechanisms, contemporary models suggest that gene-gene interactions are pivotal in determining disease initiation and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is grounded in modules of co-expressed genes across various conditions. Our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. When analyzing lipid regulation using a CRISPR screen, we find that functionally significant players are not associated but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary, by integrating co-expressed gene groups, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and identify potential targets missed by single-gene approaches. PhenoPLIER offers a novel perspective for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, facilitating the discovery of new therapeutic targets and elucidating drug mechanisms in the context of disease etiology.

              ---
               We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that synthesizes gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a unified latent representation for integrated analysis. Genes collaborate in specific contexts to perform their functions, necessitating an understanding of expression regulation across diverse conditions to elucidate the influence of these genes on complex traits. This knowledge is vital for the development of novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have shed light on the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms; however, contemporary models of the architecture of complex traits suggest that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in the origin and progression of diseases. PhenoPLIER's representation is grounded in modules of co-expressed genes across the same conditions. We find that diseases are significantly linked to gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach effectively predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Additionally, using a CRISPR screen to examine lipid regulation, we discover that functionally crucial players lack associations but are prioritized within trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary, PhenoPLIER incorporates groups of co-expressed genes to contextualize genetic associations and unveil potential targets that may be missed by single-gene approaches. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for decoding genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, thereby enhancing our understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important
              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of
              co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.

              ---
               We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. Genes collaborate in specific contexts to perform their functions, and understanding how they influence complex traits requires an appreciation of expression regulation across different conditions, crucial for developing new therapies. While transcriptome-wide association studies have elucidated the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease onset and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based on modules of co-expressed genes across similar conditions. Our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action, with diseases significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types. Using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, advancing our understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms in the context of functional genomics and gene co-expression analysis.

            text: >2-
               In the field of genetic studies, understanding the functional genomics and gene co-expression is essential for disease etiology and drug mechanisms. However, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression, making it difficult to uncover the underlying mechanisms using traditional single-gene strategies. To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. Our approach is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions, which are significantly associated with diseases in relevant cell types. Using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lacking associations are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. Our results demonstrate that by incorporating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. Overall, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, contributing to the understanding of disease etiology and drug mechanisms in functional genomics.

              ---
               We present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that synthesizes gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for integrated analysis. Genes operate in concert within specific contexts to carry out their functions; understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates comprehending expression regulation across various conditions. This comprehension is vital for designing novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have elucidated the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of the architecture of complex traits propose that gene-gene interactions are crucial for disease emergence and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is grounded in modules of co-expressed genes across the same conditions. We discover that diseases are significantly correlated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and elucidates mechanisms of action. Additionally, employing a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally significant players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In summary, integrating groups of co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and uncover potential targets overlooked by single-gene approaches. PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for decoding genetic associations through the lens of gene modules, facilitating the elucidation of disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              Keywords: genetic studies, functional genomics, gene
              co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering
              of complex traits.

              ---
               This study aims to address the gap in current research on understanding complex traits and disease mechanisms by introducing PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. The context of this research lies in the field of genetic studies and functional genomics, with a focus on gene co-expression and its role in therapeutic targets and drug repurposing. The open question that this paper seeks to answer is how to uncover the role of gene-gene interactions in disease origin and progression through the analysis of gene expression patterns across different conditions. 

              To fill this gap, we developed PhenoPLIER, a method that
              represents genes as modules with similar expression patterns under
              specific conditions. We observed that diseases are significantly
              associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and
              our approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs
              and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR
              screen to analyze lipid regulation, we found that functionally
              important players were not associated but prioritized in
              trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. 


              In conclusion, the development of PhenoPLIER provides a novel
              framework for interpreting genetic associations through the lens
              of gene modules, allowing for the contextualization of genetic
              associations and revealing potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. This research contributes to the understanding of
              complex traits and disease mechanisms by highlighting the
              importance of gene co-expression in therapeutic targets and drug
              repurposing, thereby expanding the knowledge in the fields of
              genetic studies and functional genomics.

               We present PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. Genes work together in specific contexts to perform their functions, necessitating an understanding of expression regulation across different conditions for deciphering complex trait influences. Insights into this relationship are critical for therapy development.             text: ' The study of genetic associations has long been a focus in the field of genomics, particularly in understanding complex diseases and drug mechanisms. The current state of the art, however, primarily focuses on single-gene strategies, which may overlook potential targets and drug mechanisms.               ---
               Genes collaborate to perform their functions in specific contexts, necessitating a comprehensive understanding of gene expression regulation across diverse conditions. This insight is essential for the development of novel therapies and elucidating disease-relevant mechanisms. While transcriptome-wide association studies have revealed the roles of individual genes, modern models emphasize the importance of gene-gene interactions in disease origin and progression. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is built on gene modules with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We find that diseases are significantly linked to gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and PhenoPLIER accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action. Moreover, using a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation, we discover that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER, highlighting its potential in identifying therapeutic targets and repurposing drugs.

               Genes collaborate in specific contexts to execute their functions, and understanding how these genes influence complex traits necessitates a comprehensive grasp of expression regulation across varying conditions. This comprehension is vital for the development of novel therapeutic approaches. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped elucidate the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of the architecture of complex traits postulate that gene-gene interactions are pivotal to the origin and progression of diseases. In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that synthesizes gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for integrated analysis. This representation is grounded in modules of genes displaying similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We discover that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method exhibits accuracy in predicting known drug-disease pairs and elucidating mechanisms of action. Additionally, through a CRISPR screen analyzing lipid regulation, we find that functionally significant players lack associations but are prioritized within trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.

               Genes function in coordination with one another in specific contexts to execute their tasks. Understanding how these genes impact complex traits necessitates a mechanistic comprehension of expression regulation across diverse conditions. This understanding is essential for developing new therapeutic approaches. Transcriptome-wide association studies have assisted in elucidating the role of individual genes in disease-related mechanisms. However, contemporary models of complex trait architecture predict that gene-gene interactions play a pivotal role in disease onset and progression. We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that integrates gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a shared latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is founded upon modules of genes exhibiting similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our method demonstrates accuracy in predicting known drug-disease pairs and deciphering mechanisms of action. In addition, through a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we discover that functionally significant players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.

               Understanding how genes act in concert to influence complex traits requires elucidating the mechanistic regulation of gene expression across diverse conditions, a critical aspect for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have uncovered the role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms, but modern models predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs and infer mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER, highlighting its potential in uncovering disease etiology and drug mechanisms.

              Context: The complex interplay of genes and their expression
              patterns across various conditions is critical for understanding
              the role they play in disease mechanisms and developing new
              therapies. However, existing studies have focused on individual
              gene associations, while modern models predict that gene-gene
              interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. 


              Content: To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. This representation is based on
              modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions, allowing us to analyze gene-gene interactions in
              disease mechanisms. 


              Conclusion: Our results demonstrate that PhenoPLIER accurately
              predicts known drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action.
              Moreover, using a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation, we find that
              functionally important players lacking associations are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. This
              highlights the potential of our approach in uncovering disease
              etiology and drug mechanisms, moving the broader field forward in
              understanding complex traits and their underlying genetic
              associations.

              Genes act in concert with each other in specific contexts to
              perform their functions. Determining how these genes influence
              complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression
              regulation across different conditions. It has been shown that
              this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our results
              in this study show that diseases are significantly associated with
              gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
              accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
              analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important
              players lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated
              modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of
              co-expressed genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic
              associations and reveal potential targets missed by single-gene
              strategies. PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for interpreting
              genetic associations through the lens of gene modules.

              does not provide an interpretation of the results and their

            title: >-
              Projecting genetic associations through gene expression patterns
              highlights disease etiology and drug mechanisms
            keywords: >-
              genetic studies, functional genomics, gene co-expression,
              therapeutic targets, drug repurposing, clustering of complex

            paragraph: >-
              Genes act in concert with each other in specific contexts to
              perform their functions. Determining how these genes influence
              complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression
              regulation across different conditions. It has been shown that
              this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
              Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the
              role of individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However,
              modern models of the architecture of complex traits predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression. Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational
              approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a common latent representation for a joint
              analysis. This representation is based on modules of genes with
              similar expression patterns across the same conditions. We observe
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is accurate in
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER.
